## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This is a nonlinear harmonic oscillator where acceleration (dv_dt) depends on position x, velocity v, and possibly time t. The nonlinearity can appear in the restoring force (e.g., cubic terms in x) or in the damping (e.g., velocity-dependent damping).

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Linear harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (simple restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring force with linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (undriven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Damped Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic restoring + linear damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (with periodic driving)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order restoring force)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Pendulum-like: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) (sinusoidal restoring force)
- Damped pendulum with drive: dv_dt = c0 * sin(c1 * x) + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (driven damped pendulum)
- Softening/hardening spring: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x * v**2 (position-velocity coupling)
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Cubic damping oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v**3 + c2 * v (nonlinear velocity dependence)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-modulated restoring force)
- General polynomial oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v (quadratic + cubic nonlinearity)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x³, x⁵) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium — expect odd polynomial terms in x for symmetric potentials
- Nonlinear damping terms like (1 - c*x²)*v indicate self-excited oscillations (limit cycles) as in Van der Pol systems
- Periodic driving forces appear as sin(c*t) or cos(c*t) terms added to the acceleration equation
- Position-velocity product terms x*v or x²*v indicate coupling between restoring force and dissipation mechanisms
- Even powers of x (x²) in the restoring force break symmetry and shift the equilibrium point — common in asymmetric potentials
- The sign of the cubic coefficient determines hardening (same sign as linear term's negative) vs softening spring behavior
- Absence of explicit time dependence in dv_dt indicates an autonomous system where energy considerations (conservative or dissipative) fully govern dynamics
- Rational restoring forces like x/(1 + c*x²) model bounded nonlinear potentials that saturate at large displacements

# Analysis

The Ground Truth (GT) is:
$$f(x, t, v) = 0.156062620221068 \cdot \sin(t) - 0.372947617362308 \cdot v \cdot \exp(-|x|)$$

Key features of the GT:
1. A sine term in `t` (with no phase shift, coefficient ~0.156, frequency 1)
2. A term `v * exp(-|x|)` — note the **absolute value** of x
3. No additive constant
4. No other terms

The critical challenge is the `exp(-|x|)` term. The candidates use `exp(c4*x)`, which is `exp(constant * x)`, NOT `exp(-|x|)`. The function `exp(-|x|)` is **not** the same as `exp(c*x)` for any constant `c`, because `|x|` is non-differentiable at 0 and behaves differently for positive vs negative x. Specifically:
- `exp(-|x|)` = `exp(-x)` for x > 0 and `exp(x)` for x < 0
- `exp(c*x)` is a smooth exponential for any fixed c

These are fundamentally different functions. No single `exp(c*x)` can equal `exp(-|x|)` for all x.

Let me check if any candidate has a structure that could produce `exp(-|x|)`:

Looking through all 61 candidates, they all contain terms like `exp(c*x)` (a simple exponential in x), not `exp(-|x|)`. None of them have an absolute value function.

However, let me reconsider: could any combination of terms in the candidates somehow reproduce `exp(-|x|)`? For example:
- Two exponential terms like `c3*exp(c4*x) + c5*exp(c6*x)` could potentially... no, this gives a sum of exponentials, not `v*exp(-|x|)`.
- Candidate 11 and 15 have more complex structures with divisions by `(c2*v + c3)`, but these still use `exp(c1*x)`.

None of the candidates contain `|x|` or `Abs(x)` in any form. The function `exp(-|x|)` cannot be represented as any finite combination of `exp(c*x)` terms, polynomial terms, logarithmic terms, or trigonometric terms that appear in these candidates.

**Wait** — let me reconsider the problem. Perhaps the dataset only has x ≥ 0 or the problem expects us to consider that for x ≥ 0, `exp(-|x|) = exp(-x)`, so setting c4 = -1 would work on that domain. But the problem says "for all values of the feature variables," which means all real x.

Since `exp(-|x|)` ≠ `exp(c*x)` for any constant c over all real x, **no candidate can match the GT exactly**.

But let me reconsider once more — in many physics/ML contexts, these symbolic regression results might be intended to match on a specific domain. The problem statement says "for all values of the feature variables." Under this strict interpretation, none match.

However, if we're being pragmatic and the GT uses `exp(-Abs(x))` while the candidates use `exp(c4*x)`, and if we consider this might be a notational issue where the candidates are meant to potentially represent `exp(-|x|)` through parameter choice... No, that's mathematically impossible. `c4*x` with a fixed c4 cannot equal `-|x|` for all x.

**Conclusion**: None of the candidates can match the GT because none can reproduce the `exp(-|x|)` behavior.

[NO MATCH]
